Opening Keynote: Jon McNeill and John Halamka, MD, MS

Add to schedule
Part 1: Mastering Both Innovation and Scaling: Discover the Proven Algorithm for Success As long as business has existed, people have been trying to find the secret to success, often unsuccessfully. But what if there really was a proven blueprint for growth? According to former Tesla president and Lyft COO Jon McNeill, the “algorithm for success” that’s been employed at Tesla and SpaceX has consistently delivered transformative results. In this fascinating presentation, McNeill – who led Tesla through a period of explosive growth, shares insights from his experiences and offers a deep dive into a proven method for accelerating innovation and scaling success. Through real-world examples, he unpacks the key steps of “the algorithm,” why it works, and how organizations, across industries, have leveraged it. Attendees will walk away with a practical, actionable framework they can apply immediately within their organization to drive growth and turn bold ideas into reality.  Part 2: Driving the Future of Health with Platform Innovation In Part 2 of this keynote experience, John Halamka, M.D., M.S., the Dwight and Dian Diercks President of Mayo Clinic Platform, will continue the conversation on driving and scaling healthcare innovation. Building on the concepts introduced in Part 1 of this keynote, he will discuss how collaboration within the Mayo Clinic Platform ecosystem advances innovation, data-powered insights and scalable AI solutions. Further, he will highlight the impact of Platform’s portfolio of AI-powered tools and next-generation care models at Mayo Clinic and beyond, drawing parallels to scaling breakthroughs in other industries. Attendees will leave the HIMSS26 opening keynote energized and equipped with practical strategies to lead meaningful transformation across healthcare.

AI Pavilion
Beyond the Black Box: Real-Time Voice in Healthcare with Deepgram and AWS SageMaker

Add to schedule
Voice is the most natural interface humans have ever had — yet the systems we've built in healthcare treat it like it doesn't exist. This session explores why voice remains a "black box" in clinical workflows and what it actually takes to fix it in production. Attendees will hear how deploying Deepgram's Nova-3 Medical model natively within AWS SageMaker eliminates the two barriers that kill most voice AI projects before they ship: the security risk of routing PHI outside your infrastructure, and the latency that makes AI feel like a liability instead of a tool. Whether you're a health IT leader evaluating your voice strategy or an engineer tired of stitching together fragile pipelines, this session offers a practical, human-centered look at what it takes to build systems accurate enough to trust with a drug name in a moment of crisis and fast enough that the technology finally disappears.

Government Connections Plaza | Level 1 | Booth 12526
Government Connections Plaza
Health Data Liquidity in Washington State
Washington State is poised to bring forward many modern, innovative approaches to bring true liquidity to health data for our residents. Our State HIE, HCP OneHealthPort announced this year the launch of the Washington Alliance for Health Data Exchange (WAHDX) — a collaborative statewide initiative to securely connect health, social, and research data in support of better care and stronger communities. This health data utility (HDU) enables partners across the state—including providers, community-based organizations, payers, researchers, the public, and policymakers—to securely exchange and use data for public benefit. This framework can support key initiatives from the state Medicaid and Public Health agencies in terms of providing patient’s access to their own claims and clinical data, modernizing chronic disease surveillance and leveraging the national data exchange ecosystem. This session will highlight how this new framework will leverage FHIR, SMART Health Cards/Links, individual access services, and quality measures to drive reuse, innovation and a greater ability to steward data to improve the health and wellbeing of all Washingtonians.

Patient Experience & Wellness
Reinventing Healthcare Operations: AI that helps your teams reclaim time for patient care

Add to schedule
Healthcare AI conversations often center on diagnoses and prescriptions. But there's a more immediate opportunity: freeing your teams from the administrative chaos that steals 40% of their time. You know today's reality. Clinicians lose hours to manual processes that should take minutes. Credentialing drags on for months. Simple requests bounce between departments while patients wait. These aren't just inefficiencies. They're why your best people are burning out on paperwork instead of focusing on patient care. AI offers real relief here, but not overnight and not all at once. A new generation of AI agents is tackling the repetitive work that bogs hospitals down: automating credentialing verifications, routing service requests correctly the first time, connecting fragmented systems on a single platform. Real work gets done, not just flagged for someone else to handle. This transformation requires time, thoughtful governance, and trust. But early adopters are already seeing meaningful change: clinicians reclaiming precious hours for patients, admin teams shifting from constant firefighting to strategic work, and leaders finally gaining visibility into bottlenecks they can actually fix. Join us to explore what's working today and what comes next. We'll share practical approaches for introducing AI into your workflows without breaking trust, where to find quick wins, and how to build the efficient operations your patients deserve and your teams have been waiting for.
Mar 10, 2026, 10:10 AM to 10:40 AM
Exhibition Main Stage | Level 2 | Hall A | Booth 270

Michael Vipond
Michael Vipond
ServiceNow
Artificial Intelligence in Healthcare
ServiceNow
Reinventing the Revenue Cycle with AI, Analytics, and New Benchmarks

Add to schedule
Healthcare revenue cycle leaders are confronting a perfect storm: rising denials, declining reimbursement, staff shortages, and sweeping new regulations. Recent federal regulations such as OBBBA raise the stakes by mandating real-time billing, greater price transparency, and streamlined prior authorization — regulatory shifts that require organizations to radically rethink their compliance and workflow strategies. Traditional revenue cycle metrics like “days in A/R” and “clean claim rate” no longer provide enough insight to manage these pressures. Analysis of millions of insurance claim collection activities shows that 62% of touches in the revenue cycle are wasted and 40% of denials result from pre-registration breakdowns. This hidden administrative waste translates into lost revenue, higher labor costs, and greater compliance risk under OBBBA’s tighter rules. This session will provide attendees with a practical roadmap to align, people process and technology with real case examples of how generative and agentic AI-powered tools and next-generation benchmarks have helped healthcare organizations reduce avoidable touches, increase first-touch payment rates, and unlock significant revenue improvement. Case examples include provider organizations that cut avoidable denials by up to 70% and saved hundreds of thousands annually in labor costs.

Digital Quality Measures on FHIR

Add to schedule
  Join leaders from the Centers for Medicare & Medicaid Services (CMS), the Assistant Secretary for Technology Policy (ASTP-ONC), and MultiCare Connected Care for an insightful discussion on the evolution of digital quality measures (dQMs) and opportunities for early adopters to shape the pathway for digital quality measurement. Attendees will gain valuable insights into the latest advancements and strategies, enabling them to be at the forefront of implementation. Representatives from CMS will highlight the agency’s vision for digital quality measurement, including modernization of CMS information systems and the anticipated transition from electronic clinical quality measures (eCQMs) to digital quality measures using FHIR standards. ASTP will discuss the evolving United States Core Data for Interoperability (USCDI), USCDI+ Quality and FHIR standards being evaluated for health IT certification to support quality measurement and reporting. In addition, the accountable care organization, MultiCare Connected Care, will share their experience moving to a FHIR-based digital infrastructure to streamline Medicare Shared Savings Program (MSSP) quality reporting using FHIR APIs and cloud architecture to reduce administrative burden, improve data integrity, and scale across payers and providers.

Centers for Medicare and Medicaid Services
Digital Specialty Access: Lower Costs, Higher Patient Satisfaction?

Add to schedule
Nationally, patients often face difficulties accessing in-person specialty care, resulting in delayed healthcare access and subsequent poor health outcomes. In South Carolina, all 46 counties have some health professional shortage areas. As a result, patients face exacerbated challenges accessing specialty care, averaging a 3- to 6-month wait for in-person specialty care appointments. To overcome these barriers, a 100 percent virtual-only specialty service line was developed for high-demand specialties and primary care to increase access to specialty providers and offer an alternative to in-person care. Specialty services are offered statewide, with or without a physician referral offering patients “no barrier” to services. A fully dedicated support team provides pre- and post-visit patient coordination to schedule appointments, collect demographic and pre-visit clinical information, coordinate referrals for in-person lab work, imaging, and pharmaceuticals based on the patient's location, and reduce patient no-shows by assisting patients in connecting to their virtual visit. This coordination results in an increase in overall patient satisfaction compared to hybrid in-person/virtual care.

Embedding Clinical Intelligence to Transform Medicare Shared Savings Program Outcomes at Scale

Add to schedule
Improving performance in the Medicare Shared Savings Program (MSSP) requires more than retrospective analytics or clinician education. This session examines the impact of integrating risk adjustment and quality gap closure prompts directly into clinical workflows across a complex ambulatory network. The intervention led to a projected $14.9 million in shared savings, driven by a 20-percent improvement in HCC revalidation and 22 percent more quality gaps closed. Attendees will explore how aligning decision support with routine care delivery improves documentation accuracy, supports pre-visit planning, and enables physicians to meet MSSP performance thresholds without added administrative burden. The session offers a replicable model for enhancing financial and clinical outcomes in value-based care environments through embedded intelligence and physician-centered design.

From Intention to Results: Optimizing Leadership Development to Transform Workforce

Add to schedule
Today’s healthcare leaders are operating within a complex environment marked by ongoing workforce challenges, rising consumer expectations and rapid digital transformation. In this climate, leadership development is no longer optional – it is essential to building the competencies, culture, and resilience needed for healthcare organizations to thrive. To this end, AdventHealth has made leadership development a strategic priority – reflected by its inclusion within the organization’s 10-year strategic roadmap called Vision 2030.  A key driver of workforce development is its award-winning Leadership Institute, guided by its Lead Self, Lead Others, Lead Results framework. Its scalable model supports leaders at every level — from frontline and clinical managers to senior executives – and aligns leadership practices with both organizational goals and workforce needs. Through technology-enabled access across our nine-state system, its programs have delivered measurable outcomes, including effectiveness scores well above industry benchmarks. Drawing from both formal programs and real-world innovation and technology initiatives, this session will explore how intentional, enterprise-wide leadership development can build a culture that attracts and retains a mission driven-workforce – one that is resilient, prepared, and skilled to navigate disruption and lead in today’s complex, technology-driven healthcare environment.

Full Stack AI for Healthcare in Action: Optimizing Clinical Workflows with Conversational AI for Prior Auth

Add to schedule
Prior authorization remains one of the most significant contributors to clinician burnout and care delays, costing the U.S. healthcare system billions in administrative waste. While traditional automation has struggled with the messy reality of clinical documentation, the emergence of Agentic Conversational AI has created a paradigm shift. This session moves beyond the AI hype to demonstrate real outcomes of AI for Healthcare. We explore the core technology building blocks to build, run, govern, secure and scale AI apps and agents. We look at best practices to handle agent identity and agent governance. We also focus on how a specific outcome; conversational AI agents, integrated directly into EHR workflows,now navigate the complexities of medical necessity by interpreting nuanced clinical notes and engaging in multi-turn dialogues with payer systems. Lets build the future of AI in healthcare together.

Artificial Intelligence in Healthcare
WSO2
Integrating Data-Driven Workflows to Prevent Workplace Violence

Add to schedule
This session will highlight Parkland Health's innovative approach to mitigating workplace violence (WPV) in inpatient settings. WPV is a significant concern in healthcare, with health and social service workers five times more likely to be injured than other workers. Between 8 percent and 38 percent of healthcare workers globally experience physical violence and many more face verbal aggression. Despite this, the true magnitude of WPV often goes unnoticed, leading to inadequate prevention measures. The session will detail the development and implementation of a predictive model designed to identify potentially violent patients in inpatient settings. The workflow driven by this predictive model integrates directly into the nursing process. Upon patient admission, the Parkland Center For Clinical Innovation (PCCI) Model triggers a “brain task” for patients identified as needing a Bröset Violence Checklist (BVC) assessment. Nurses then document witnessed behaviors from the six-item BVC (attacking objects, physical threats, verbal threats, boisterous, irritable, confused). Based on the BVC score, “Our Practice Advisory” guides nurses on appropriate interventions and reassessment frequencies. This proactive system aims to empower healthcare workers to take additional safety measures and reduce the likelihood of WPV incidents.
Mar 10, 2026, 10:15 AM to 11:15 AM
Level 5 | Palazzo C
Education Sessions
Jacqueline Naeem
Jacqueline Naeem

Brett Moran
Brett Moran

Artificial Intelligence in Healthcare
Internal Alignment to Early Results: One Health System's Post-Acute Transformation

Add to schedule
Managing patients across the post-acute continuum--entering, residing in, and transitioning out of skilled nursing facilities--has long challenged health systems. Limited visibility into patient status and fragmented workflows often lead to delays, inefficiencies, and missed opportunities. One large multi-state health system recognized that improving care management required a new approach: one providing real-time insights and connecting clinical, operational, and IT teams beyond the EHR. In this session, organization leaders will share how they identified gaps in care transitions and developed a strategy to address them. You'll hear how they partnered with IT to align on necessary capabilities beyond their tech stack, secured buy-in, and integrated new solutions without disrupting workflows. This journey is focused not just on technology, but on collaboration that supports proactive discharge planning, reduces delays, and strengthens continuity of care. We'll explore early results and lessons learned, including how enhanced visibility enables the teams to tackle post-acute care management challenges. Discussion will also touch on empowering ED providers with insight into relevant clinical information for patients returning from a SNF, and how these efforts complement post-acute strategies.  Attendees will gain practical insights on building consensus, overcoming barriers, and advancing care management.

Interop+Smart Experience
Mastering Healthcare ROI: From Basic Analytics to Artificial Intelligence-Powered Precision Targeting

Add to schedule
Healthcare organizations invest billions in interventions yet struggle to quantify true return on investment. This workshop demystifies ROI measurement, providing attendees with a practical toolkit ranging from simple to sophisticated approaches. We'll begin with pre/post analysis—the workhorse method that addresses 75 percent of ROI use cases with straightforward implementation. Next, we’ll explore cohort matching and control groups, examining when this added complexity delivers value versus creating dimensionality challenges that limit scalability. Building in complexity, we’ll tackle difference-in-differences methodology, discussing why its theoretical elegance often conflicts with stakeholder needs for interpretable dollar-value outcomes. Finally, we’ll demonstrate cutting-edge x-learner techniques that enable individual-level ROI predictions, transforming population averages into precision targeting that identifies hidden high-value subpopulations. Through hands-on examples and real-world case studies, attendees will learn to select the right ROI approach for their context, balancing analytical rigor with practical constraints. Whether you’re a healthcare system executive, payer analyst or population health manager, you’ll leave equipped to demonstrate intervention value, optimize resource allocation, and build compelling business cases that secure sustainable funding for programs that matter. Take-home: Master the ROI measurement spectrum to prove program value and drive data-informed healthcare decisions.

Stakeholder Governance Strategies for Ambient Artificial Intelligence Scribes: An Interactive Workshop

Add to schedule
Ambient artificial intelligence (AI) Scribe applications are rapidly emerging technologies in healthcare environments, and healthcare organizations are currently piloting implementations. However, several questions have arisen from each of the key stakeholders. There is uncertainty regarding patient understanding, the need for frequent consent and reconsent, and privacy concerns. Clinicians are expressing hope for greater patient engagement during clinical encounters and reduced “pajama time,” but are mindful of workflow disruptions and the potential inaccuracies and fallibility of generative AI. Similarly, information technologists recognize the need for validations, business rules and ongoing alignment with health IT strategy. However, many of these considerations have not yet been established, resulting in a lack of supporting documentation. The goal of this workshop is to collect practices utilized by healthcare organizations from the patient, clinician and information technologist perspectives, to formulate ambient AI scribe governance best practices for each. Objectives include identifying impactful benefits and unintended consequences of Ambient AI Scribes, articulating AI governance strategies for the stakeholders, and constructing documentation and analysis expectations for Ambient AI Scribe implementation. Workshop participants will take away strategies for honoring the unique considerations and organizational best practices to promote trust for each of these stakeholders.

Artificial Intelligence in Healthcare
Successful Patient Incident Investigations of Intelligent and Artificial Intelligence Systems

Add to schedule
Investigating patient harm or death involving intelligent or AI-based devices and systems requires specialized approaches. These technologies form a complex System of Systems, where devices, software and firmware interact in dynamic and often unpredictable ways, influenced by configurations, updates and application settings. Semi- and fully autonomous systems further complicate causality assessments. Effective investigation demands rapid, skilled system analysis and documentation to determine root causes and implement timely remediation. A key challenge is preserving the “as-was” state of all involved technologies and the incident environment before potential reconfiguration or automatic updates occur. Investigators must act fast to document and secure components—such as smart infusion pumps, order entry systems, and integrated EHRs—since these systems are highly interdependent and subject to asynchronous changes by vendors, users, clinical engineers, biomedical technicians, and IT professionals. Once root causes are fully understood, necessary remediation will likely require well-documented technical interventions and both clinical and technical specialist training. This session outlines essential steps and success factors for conducting thorough, timely forensic investigations and remediation in today’s AI-driven healthcare environment.

Wait, I'm the Human in the Loop?

Add to schedule
“Human in the loop” is everywhere in AI policy and vendor promises — but what does it actually mean when applied in healthcare? Too often, the label shifts risk onto clinicians and leaders without giving them the tools, context, or authority to act effectively. Meanwhile, the “learned intermediary” model raises similar questions: who carries responsibility, how is oversight documented, and when is it more symbolic than substantive? This session unpacks the real implications of HITL and learned intermediary models in healthcare AI. Using AI-generated reproductions of recent scenarios from operations, extreme weather and disaster repsone, we will explore when oversight empowers safe, explainable decisions — and when it risks becoming a liability handoff. We present a clear-eyed landscape of options and trade-offs: where oversight works, where it falters, opportunities to strengthen it, and risks if left unchecked. Attendees will leave with a framework for complex operational decision triage, and sharper awareness of how HITL and learned intermediary models are evolving, how to identify red flags, and how to ask better questions about liability, workflow, and training before assuming “human in the loop” is enough.

Digital Health Transformation: Connecting Clinical and Public Health Systems

Add to schedule
Digital health transformation relies on successful interoperability between clinical and public health systems. The American Immunization Registry Association (AIRA) drives national progress through its Measurement and Improvement (M&I) Initiative and Immunization Integration Program (IIP), demonstrating how collaborative, standards-based testing strengthens data quality and advances public health outcomes. This session highlights AIRA's coordinated approach to advancing interoperability, showcasing how HIMSS and AIRA amplify achievements of immunization information systems (IIS), health IT vendors, and partners transforming data exchange. The IIP—a partnership between CDC, AIRA, HIMSS, and Drummond—tests and recognizes EHRs with advanced immunization capabilities supporting data exchange with public health IIS. The M&I Initiative provides a community-driven framework to measure and validate IIS across multiple content areas, supporting continuous modernization. AIRA has expanded its scope to include vendor product testing, assessing products and modules to inform design enhancements and help jurisdictions make strategic decisions.

Denoising Healthcare AI: Consummate Search, Observability, Security

Add to schedule
As telemetry volumes and alert noise continue to grow, SOCs are overwhelmed by a set of persistent pain points: alert fatigue and high false‑positive rates that bury real threats, stretched analyst capacity and chronic burnout, long mean time to detect and respond (MTTD/MTTR), fractured telemetry and enrichment workflows, and slow, manual investigations that leave gaps in coverage and compliance. These inefficiencies not only increase risk exposure but also drive up operational cost and erode analyst trust in tooling. This session zeroes in on how AI-driven detection addresses those exact pain points. You’ll see how correlated adversary activity surfaced can collapse noisy alerts into focused, high‑value investigations, automate enrichment to reclaim analyst time, and improve signal‑to‑noise so teams detect and respond faster.

As patient financial responsibility grows, healthcare organizations have rapidly digitized payment intake across payer portals, patient portals, HSAs, financing platforms, and virtual card programs. Add to schedule

Empowering Patients, Enabling Life-Saving Care: TEFCA, 360X Interoperability, and AI-Enabled IAS

Add to schedule
A 39-year-old woman with new psychiatric symptoms visits her PCP, who initiates a 360X closed-loop referral to psychiatry. As her symptoms rapidly progress, the psychiatrist identifies concern for an underlying life-threatening condition and urgently transfers her to the ED. In the ED, clinicians query her medical information using TEFCA QHIN-enabled interoperability. She receives timely treatment, makes a full recovery, and retains little memory of the acute event. After returning home, she logs into her HealthEx application. Her identity is verified through CLEAR, enabling secure access. Her data is retrieved via TEFCA interoperability, allowing her to view a comprehensive record of her care. Using AI-enabled tools within the application, she is able to clearly understand her medical history and what occurred during her illness.

Ambient Nursing Documentation Tool Built for Nurses, By Nurses

Add to schedule
The Ambient Nursing Documentation initiative is a nurse-designed innovation that leverages conversational-based artificial intelligence (AI) to support inpatient documentation. Built for MedSurg and Progressive Care Unit settings, the tool passively captures nurse-patient conversations and files relevant data into discrete fields in the electronic health record. This solution reduces screen time and administrative workload, enabling nurses to focus on delivering patient-centered care. Codeveloped with frontline nurses and tested through a rigorous Institutional Review Board-validated process across seven inpatient units, this technology demonstrates the potential to transform the nursing experience and improve documentation quality. Preliminary findings show strong adoption among both nurses and patients. The tool's development is for nurses, by nurses, and is supported by robust change management strategies. This session will provide insight into the Ambient Nursing Documentation tool and how a nursing-led innovation strategy can effectively lay the groundwork for scalable transformation in clinical documentation.

BEST IM Program: Accelerating the Automation of Adverse Event Reporting

Add to schedule
The FDA Center for Biologics Evaluation and Research(CBER) is expanding its pilot program for health systems participating in automated reporting of potential adverse events (AEs) of vaccines, blood products, gene therapies and other biologics. The Biologics Effectiveness and Safety (BEST) Innovative Methods (IM) Program enables health systems to transfer data from electronic health records to the FDA using Fast Healthcare Interoperability Resources standards through the national eHealth Exchange. Electronic phenotypes specify electronic health record data elements needed to identify and report potential adverse events such as anaphylaxis, hypogammaglobulinemia, myocarditis/pericarditis and aseptic meningitis. FDA studies from 2024 and 2025 demonstrate the use of AI, large language models and logic tools using Clinical Quality Language to greatly accelerate the systematic approach to evaluating AEs and improving patient safety surveillance. The FDA is expanding the program to cover additional phenotypes and many more healthcare systems across the United States.

Workforce
Equitable Healthcare: Bias-Free Algorithms Reducing Costly Care Disparities

Add to schedule
This project addresses algorithmic bias in commercial EHR algorithms that can exacerbate healthcare disparities across sociodemographic groups. Using two real-world clinical classification models—one predicting asthma-related emergency department visits and the other unplanned readmissions—our team evaluated two post-processing bias mitigation methods to reduce differences in false negative rates across race/ethnicity, sex, language and insurance. After reviewing the literature and pilot testing the most frequently cited methods, threshold adjustment was identified as the most effective approach. Threshold adjustment maintained model accuracy and alert rates while significantly reducing bias, as measured by Equal Opportunity Difference. Sparse and outdated documentation of existing open-source bias mitigation tools prompted the development of an in-house R code that enhanced both transparency and bias reduction. The project culminated in an open-source playbook and code repository to guide other health systems with limited resources in applying these methods. This work demonstrates a low-resource pathway to mitigating algorithmic bias in healthcare applications, with potential for broad application in safety-net and other under-resourced systems. Attendees will gain insights on practical bias mitigation strategies, real-world implementation challenges, and how to leverage the project’s open-source playbook to promote health equity in AI-driven clinical decision support.

From Data to Foresight: Modernizing Public Health Intelligence

Add to schedule
This session features Dr. Jason Asher and CAPT Matt Ritchey discussing CDC’s public health data and data science modernization efforts. Data modernization is a top priority for CDC and at the heart of a national effort to create integrated, real-time health data and surveillance that can protect us from any threat. Public health infrastructure has been largely structured around outbreak detection and response. CDC is working with others to shift this towards forecasting and anticipation by building out the technical infrastructure and innovation needed to make disease forecasting, modeling, and simulation a regular part of public health. Hospital-at-Home: Financial Benefits and Superior Member Satisfaction

Add to schedule
The godfather of Hospital-at-Home, Dr. Bruce Leff projected, “One day, hospitals will just be ERs, intensive care units, and operating rooms. Everyone else will be treated at home.” Waiting to see how this plays out may put healthcare systems at a disadvantage. They must evaluate Hospital-at-Home’s role within their enterprise. Given hospital-reimbursement-parity under Centers for Medicare and Medicaid Services (CMS) waiver and bi-Congress legislation, Hospital-at-Home’s a pragmatic starting point. However, most struggle with determining program feasibility in the first place and how to scale. Of the 330 hospitals with the waiver, we estimate 50 percent have launched and fewer have scaled their programs. Hear from one of the biggest U.S. Hospital-at-Home operations on how to dispel common myths that weaken the business case, and discrete ways Hospital-at-Home creates financial value. They’ll outline how to build the business case and how to scale the program. Learn success factors and an actionable framework to apply in your organization.

Putting Patients First: Implementing Patient Cost Transparency Using HL7® FHIR®

Add to schedule
In February 2025, President Trump issued a new Executive Order on healthcare pricing transparency, signaling that the federal government is planning on stronger enforcement and clearer expectations for patient transparency to make informed healthcare decisions. Since the 2021 enactment of the No Surprises Act, which sought to protect consumers from surprise medical bills arising out of certain out-of-network emergency care, a multistakeholder, industry-driven initiative has been working on a standardized approach to patient cost transparency implementation. In this session you will learn about the U.S. healthcare ecosystem’s renewed efforts to make systemic changes to promote transparency and align incentives to empower patients to use their health data to make informed decisions. Discover how providers, payers and vendors are collaborating and harnessing HL7® FHIR® to automate and streamline processes and improve data exchange for patient cost transparency. Learn about the industry initiative’s work on Good Faith Estimates data exchange between providers and hear about the progress of early adopter pilot projects. Learn how their collective efforts will ultimately provide more efficient coordination, faster processing, and enable accurate, real-time access via apps to the cost of medical care prior to delivery, allowing patients to make better healthcare decisions.

Rapid Response: Implementing the Fraud Defense Operations Center

Add to schedule
In 2025, the Center for Program Integrity within the Centers for Medicare and Medicaid Services implemented the Fraud Defense Operations Center (FDOC). The purpose of this center was to address fraud risk in near real time by bringing together analysts, investigators, law enforcement, and compliance/regulatory experts. In total, the FDOC triaged over 340 suspect providers and took swift action to prevent payment of over $1.4 billion while fraud investigations continued. The FDOC serves as a model to prevent fraud losses through targeted analytics and data-driven decision making.

Virtual Nursing: Redefining the Bedside Experience through Virtual Innovation

Add to schedule
Piedmont Healthcare launched a virtual nursing pilot to address the nursing shortage and improve patient care. Over 90 days, 143 in-room devices were deployed, resulting in improved nurse satisfaction, reduced discharge times, and enhanced patient experience. Encouraged by these outcomes, the program expanded to 17 hospitals with over 2,700 devices in 10 months. Within 18 months, Piedmont achieved full 24/7 virtual RN coverage. Key metrics showed improvements in medication review timeliness (7.8 hours faster), discharge order-to-door time (81 minutes faster), and ED hold times (1.3 hours shorter). Nurse satisfaction surveys revealed 84% of bedside nurses “like or love” virtual nursing, and 78% are more likely to stay at Piedmont. This innovative model has transformed care delivery, reduced excess patient days, and improved operational efficiency across the system.

Will Artificial Intelligence Help or Hinder Advancing Sustainable Healthcare?

Add to schedule
The integration of artificial intelligence (AI) into healthcare presents both opportunities and risks for sustainability. This workshop will provide attendees with a nuanced understanding of how AI can either accelerate progress toward environmentally sustainable healthcare or exacerbate its carbon footprint. Through brief presentations and interactive activities, participants will explore: (1) the potential for AI to optimize clinical workflows, reduce waste and improve resource allocation; and (2) the energy and environmental costs of AI-driven healthcare systems, including the carbon footprint of model training and inference. The workshop will employ an inclusive and participatory design-thinking methodology, enabling attendees to contribute to the development of best practices for deploying AI sustainably in healthcare. A large-group activity will focus on assessing AI’s sustainability impact across different healthcare domains such as radiology, digital documentation and predictive analytics. By the end of the session, participants will leave with practical frameworks for evaluating the environmental trade-offs of AI in healthcare and strategies for implementing AI in a way that aligns with decarbonization goals.

Fax Forward: How Agentic AI is Transforming Fax Workflows

Add to schedule
Fax remains healthcare’s most common communication channel - with more than one-third of healthcare documents still arriving by fax and over half requiring manual intervention before they can be processed. This leaves providers buried in paperwork and working after hours to keep up. Misaligned incentives and fragmented systems have caused decades of digitization to fall short. In this session, you’ll see how agentic AI is finally breaking that cycle - transforming inbound faxes into intelligent, validation-ready workflows that reduce administrative burden and enable faster, more efficient operations. Discover how this shift is already happening today and what it means for the future of healthcare workflows.

Empowering Patients, Enabling Life-Saving Care: TEFCA, 360X Interoperability, and AI-Enabled IAS

Add to schedule
A 39-year-old woman with new psychiatric symptoms visits her PCP, who initiates a 360X closed-loop referral to psychiatry. As her symptoms rapidly progress, the psychiatrist identifies concern for an underlying life-threatening condition and urgently transfers her to the ED. In the ED, clinicians query her medical information using TEFCA QHIN-enabled interoperability. She receives timely treatment, makes a full recovery, and retains little memory of the acute event. After returning home, she logs into her HealthEx application. Her identity is verified through CLEAR, enabling secure access. Her data is retrieved via TEFCA interoperability, allowing her to view a comprehensive record of her care. Using AI-enabled tools within the application, she is able to clearly understand her medical history and what occurred during her illness.

Interop+Smart Experience | Level 1 | The Park (Hall G) | Booth 12511
Interop+Smart Experience
Healthcare Needs a Better Third-Party Risk Assessment Approach

Add to schedule
Modern healthcare relies on growing numbers of third-party vendors, suppliers, and partners providing critical functions across healthcare delivery. When one third party is cyber-attacked, repercussions can be alarmingly broad and devastating—the Synnovis and Change Healthcare attacks demonstrate impacts on patient morbidity, mortality, and financial stability. Expecting providers to risk-assess thousands of partners annually is unrealistic. This presentation examines the need for a different approach: placing the onus to be secure and compliant upon third parties, establishing common audit and assessment frameworks across healthcare, and wider use of attestation frameworks like SOC 2 Type II as improved indicators of security and resiliency.

Securing Payer Interoperability at Scale: FAST Security + Da Vinci in Action Across CMS-Aligned Networks

Add to schedule
As CMS accelerates the Health Technology Ecosystem and CMS-Aligned Networks initiative, payers and providers must move from isolated APIs to secure, network-to-network interoperability at scale. This session demonstrates how HL7® FHIR® at Scale Taskforce (FAST) Security STU 2, in collaboration with the HL7 Da Vinci Project, provides the standardized trust framework required to operationalize payer interoperability across CMS-0057, prior authorization, payer-to-payer exchange, and TEFCA-facilitated FHIR. Led by FAST Technical Director, David Pyke, the session will explain how certificate-based digital identity, dynamic client registration, OAuth-based authorization, and automated trust onboarding create repeatable, scalable API security patterns across networks. Mark Scrimshire will bring implementation perspective from OnyxHealth, illustrating how these standards are applied in real-world payer environments to support prior authorization workflows, directory-driven API discovery, payer-to-payer exchange, and production FHIR deployments aligned with Da Vinci implementation guides. Speakers: David Pyke, Technical Director, HL7 FAST FHIR Accelerator Mark Scrimshire, Co-Chair, HL7 Da Vinci Project Payer Data Exchange Work Group; Chief Interoperability and Innovation Officer, Onyx Health

Interop+Smart Experience
From Signal to System: Operationalizing Wastewater-Based Epidemiology for Infectious Disease Surveillance

Add to schedule
Wastewater-based epidemiology (WBE) expanded rapidly during the COVID-19 response and demonstrated value as a complementary, population-level surveillance input for infectious diseases. As public health agencies advance long-term data modernization, the focus is on what it takes to operate wastewater surveillance routinely, reliably, consistently, and at scale. These requirements include data quality and method comparability, interoperability with existing public health and healthcare data systems, clear governance and responsible-use practices, coverage limitations in rural/tribal and decentralized sanitation contexts, and financing stability to maintain core operational capacity. In this session, we will summarize key gaps and policy levers identified in current WBE implementation and translate them into an actionable framework for federal, state, local, and tribal leadership. The session will focus on what is feasible now: standardizing minimum datasets and QA/QC expectations, improving integration into routine surveillance workflows, clarifying roles across public health agencies, utilities, and laboratories, and identifying implementation considerations for expanding coverage and sustaining capacity. Participants will leave with a structured way to evaluate WBE programs and prioritize next steps aligned with public health data modernization goals. Learning Objectives Learning Objective #1 Identify major operational gaps that limit the routine use of wastewater-based epidemiology for infectious disease surveillance. Learning Objective #2 Describe practical policy levers available to federal, state, local, and tribal leadership to improve WBE implementation. Learning Objective #3 Apply a tiered implementation roadmap to prioritize near-term actions for institutionalizing wastewater data within routine surveillance workflows and aligning it with broader public health data modernization efforts.

Time Transparency: What Hospitals Can Learn from Domino's Pizza Tracker

Add to schedule
From tracking a pizza from the oven to your doorstep to getting texted when it's your turn for a haircut, consumers have come to expect knowing precisely when something will occur. Unfortunately, this expectation is abandoned when it matters the most. Hospital rooms are expensive waiting rooms. Not knowing when to expect the doctors for rounds makes it nearly impossible to implement the best-practice of including nurses, patients, and families in the most important discussion of the day. When nurses and families are present for rounds, medical errors decrease, patient and nurse satisfaction increases, and hospitals run more efficiently.  In this session, Dr. Michael Pitt, a pediatric hospitalist and co-founder and CEO of Q-rounds, will share how hospitals can leverage Time Transparency to automate the inclusion of all stakeholders for daily rounds, in person or virtually. KF
Kyle Farmer
Workforce
Empowering Patients, Enabling Life-Saving Care: TEFCA, 360X Interoperability, and AI-Enabled IAS

Add to schedule
A 39-year-old woman with new psychiatric symptoms visits her PCP, who initiates a 360X closed-loop referral to psychiatry. As her symptoms rapidly progress, the psychiatrist identifies concern for an underlying life-threatening condition and urgently transfers her to the ED. In the ED, clinicians query her medical information using TEFCA QHIN-enabled interoperability. She receives timely treatment, makes a full recovery, and retains little memory of the acute event. After returning home, she logs into her HealthEx application. Her identity is verified through CLEAR, enabling secure access. Her data is retrieved via TEFCA interoperability, allowing her to view a comprehensive record of her care. Using AI-enabled tools within the application, she is able to clearly understand her medical history and what occurred during her illness.

From Pilot to Production: AI Governance and Regulatory Readiness in Global Healthcare

Add to schedule
Hospitals and health systems globally are embracing artificial intelligence (AI) to deliver high-quality healthcare efficiently while supporting provider and patient empowerment. The session explores formal AI governance policies, regulatory compliance, and regional differences, while examining universal barriers and opportunities including security concerns, auditing processes, clinician autonomy in AI-assisted decision-making, and AI vendor selection criteria and management processes.

Frontline Innovation: How Non-IT Teams Are Building AI Workflows

Add to schedule
While most healthcare AI initiatives are IT-led, this session highlights a different path—frontline teams building and launching automations themselves. The Chief Digital Transformation Officer and Program Manager for AI Agents at a large academic medical center share how they created a collaborative framework with IT to enable no-code workflow development. By establishing processes for data feed integration, QA, governance, and outcome measurement, the organization empowered staff to launch AI-powered workflows quickly and safely without burdening technical teams. Attendees learn how digital transformation and IT partnered to identify high-value use cases, enable secure data access, and reduce typical six-month implementation timelines to weeks. The session offers practical insights into democratizing automation through low-code tools and building guardrails ensuring safety, scalability, and sustainability, including early wins, governance structures, and expansion plans.

Broadcom Inc.
Your EHR is Stealing Time From Care

Add to schedule
For decades, EHRs have stolen time from care—prioritizing documentation over delivery and forcing clinicians to work around technology instead of being supported by it. As ambulatory care faces unprecedented pressure, burnout, and inefficiency, incremental optimization is no longer enough. We have reached an inflection point that demands rethinking the EHR as a foundation for care delivery, not merely a system of record.  This session explores designing an agentic ambulatory care platform built around the clinical encounter. Rather than layering AI onto legacy systems, this approach reimagines the entire care journey—from pre-visit preparation to post-visit follow-up—so technology assumes the administrative burden clinicians currently carry.  Attendees will learn why fragmented workflows cannot be fixed by improving individual features, and how intentional design enables automation at scale. We’ll examine real-world impact, including measurable reductions in administrative time and missed steps in care delivery.  Most importantly, this model changes the experience of care itself. When technology fades into the background, clinicians and patients regain face time, decisions happen in real time, and care becomes more human. This session is for healthcare leaders ready to move beyond AI promises toward a new technology category designed for how care is actually delivered.

Add to schedule

InsighTCROSS is an AI-driven decision-support software developed to eliminate such waste and maximize sales revenue. In this session, we will introduce the platform’s new capability to predict and identify physicians with a high likelihood of adopting newly launched drugs—a task traditionally considered extremely difficult. Integrating Workforce, Payroll, and Dining Systems in Healthcare: Operational Results That Matter

Add to schedule
Healthcare organizations are under relentless pressure to do more with less while meeting rising expectations from employees, patients, and guests. Fragmented systems quietly drain productivity, increase risk, and erode trust. Integrated digital platforms change that math. This session explores how unifying workforce technology, payroll data exchange, and retail dining systems delivers measurable operational and financial results. Attendees will learn how badge-based employee pay programs reduce cash handling, speed transactions, and drive adoption, with organizations reporting transaction times cut by over 30 percent and employee satisfaction scores rising alongside participation. We will examine how secure, automated data transfer for payroll deductions reduces reconciliation errors by up to 80 percent while strengthening compliance and audit readiness. The discussion also dives into the next generation of healthcare retail dining. Bring your own device ordering for patients, guests, and staff is improving throughput, increasing average ticket size by double digits, and enhancing patient experience scores without adding labor. When dining, workforce pay, and payroll systems operate as one ecosystem, healthcare leaders gain real-time insight, stronger security, and a more resilient operation. Attendees will leave with practical strategies, outcome-driven benchmarks, and a clear roadmap for using integrated digital tools to improve efficiency, engagement, and trust across the healthcare enterprise.

Attendees will gain insights into practical, real-world strategies for: Mass Digitization and Curation: Successfully transforming vast, historical archives—specifically in digital pathology—from secure physical handling to high-quality whole-slide imaging and accurate, standardized metadata tagging. Intelligent Data Economics: Implementing tiered, intelligent storage solutions that optimize data placement based on access frequency and regulatory requirements, driving cost efficiencies and ensuring rapid retrieval for clinical and research needs. Creating AI-Ready Datasets: Establishing best practices for generating large, properly de-identified, and highly curated datasets essential for training robust AI models while meticulously protecting patient privacy and ensuring compliance. Facilitating Ethical Data Exchange: Leveraging a trusted, neutral framework to accelerate medical innovation through ethical data sharing, ensuring data contributors maintain transparency and control over how their valuable assets are utilized.

Enhancing Diagnostic Efficiency and Patient Experience Through Operational Resource Innovation

Add to schedule
Faced with a surge in patient diagnostic tests—with some exam volumes increasing by more than 90 percent in a decade—Samsung Medical Center's operational models were under significant strain, leading to workflow bottlenecks and potential delays in care. This session outlines the development and implementation of a data-driven analytics tool designed to proactively manage these challenges. We will showcase how this centralized data delivery tool (PAN) led to significant, measurable improvements. Key findings include a 14.1 percent increase in MRI reservation efficiency, a 7.5 percent increase in echocardiography throughput, and the ability to perform an average of seven additional CT scans daily. The system also resolved long patient wait times in blood collection rooms by using predictive analytics for optimized manpower allocation, reducing average wait times that exceeded 10 minutes to under 8 minutes. The take-home message is that a proactive, data-driven approach to managing clinical operations can transform hospital efficiency and enhance patient care. This case study provides a practical model for how other healthcare institutions can leverage predictive analytics to optimize resource utilization, improve patient flow and safety, and build a more resilient care delivery system.

Global Progress Toward Digital Transformation in the Post-Pandemic Era

Add to schedule
The COVID-19 pandemic accelerated digital health adoption worldwide, but how far have healthcare organizations actually progressed in their digital transformation journeys? This session presents comprehensive analysis from the HIMSS Office of Scientific Research, examining Digital Health Indicator (DHI) data from 253 healthcare organizations across 12 countries, revealing striking global patterns in digital maturity development. The research uncovers significant variations in digital readiness across regions, with notable differences between developed and developing healthcare systems. Most remarkably, the data reveals that governance and workforce capacity consistently rank as the strongest digital health capability globally, while person-enabled health and predictive analytics lag significantly behind across all countries. Through analysis of interoperability, person-enabled health, predictive analytics and governance capabilities, this session examines what these patterns reveal about global digital health priorities and readiness. The findings highlight critical gaps where healthcare organizations worldwide are struggling to advance, particularly in patient engagement technologies and data-driven decision-making. Drawing on self-reported assessments from diverse healthcare systems, this session provides evidence-based insights into where the global healthcare community stands in the post-pandemic digital transformation era and identifies universal challenges that transcend national boundaries.

Innovating with INSIGHT: Best Practices for Evaluating Emerging Health Technologies

Add to schedule
In an era of rapid healthcare tech innovation, healthcare leaders face a critical challenge: choosing which emerging technologies will truly benefit their organizations. This session presents a structured, evidence-based evaluation framework designed to fill that gap, replacing ad-hoc, hype-driven choices with data-driven decisions. Using standardized criteria and practical tools (like an innovation heatmap and scoring calculator), this framework objectively assesses new tech opportunities by their value and implementation difficulty. The Innovation Scoring and Impact Guide for Healthcare Technologies (INSIGHT) was developed to quantitatively score a given innovation’s “readiness” or merit. Findings from pilot use show that applying this approach helps prioritize high-impact, feasible innovations while avoiding those that are misaligned or high-risk. The key takeaway is that adopting a consistent evaluation toolkit and best practices enables smarter technology decisions aligned with strategic goals and better patient outcomes.

Intrapreneurship: Who Owns the Idea?

Add to schedule
Intrapreneurship empowers innovators within organizations to identify challenges and create solutions that transform care, processes, and systems. Unlike entrepreneurs, intrapreneurs operate within existing structures and rely on institutional resources — raising the central question: who owns the idea? This session explores the tension between individual creativity and organizational ownership, emphasizing how recognition, transparency, and clear policies influence whether innovators feel valued and supported. Frontline employees generate insights from lived experiences, while organizations provide the funding, infrastructure, and scale necessary to bring those ideas forward. Ownership, therefore, is best understood as a partnership rather than a competition. When ideas are co-owned, organizations build trust, foster innovation, and ensure lasting impact. The talk will also highlight how one health system encourages intrapreneurship through defined pathways to commercialization, engagement with the technology transfer office, and consideration of intellectual property, patents, and copyright. Ultimately, participants will gain practical insights into how intrapreneurship can unlock creativity, strengthen collaboration, and sustain meaningful change within complex systems.

Managing Systemic Risk in a Digitized Healthcare Ecosystem

Add to schedule
In Collaboration With:   Healthcare's interconnected ecosystem—spanning patient care, payments, pharmaceuticals, technology, and public health—creates cascading cybersecurity risks. A single ransomware attack on one supplier can shut down nationwide healthcare delivery, compromising patient data, payment systems, and medical devices. To address this vulnerability, the Health Sector Coordinating Cybersecurity Working Group released the Sector Mapping and Risk Management Toolkit (SMART) in October. SMART provides actionable guidance for managing systemic risks and critical dependencies across health systems. It empowers organizations to demand secure products and high-availability services from suppliers, driving improved security standards ecosystem-wide. When customer leverage is insufficient to influence third-party security, SMART helps organizations anticipate incidents and develop backup plans.

Securing the Edge: Protecting Our Hospital

Add to schedule
Endorsed by: Hospitals are increasingly reliant on a vast and diverse ecosystem of edge devices—ranging from mobile workstations and tablets to infusion pumps and diagnostic equipment. Yet, these devices often operate with limited oversight, outdated software and weak access controls, making them a prime target for attackers. In this session, we will share a comprehensive case study on how we tackled edge device vulnerabilities and reshaped our security posture from the ground up. The session will begin with an overview of why edge security is particularly critical in a healthcare setting and the unique threats posed by legacy and unmanaged medical devices. We’ll walk through the results of our initial risk assessment, which revealed more than 10,000 edge devices and multiple categories of vulnerabilities, including hardcoded credentials and vendor-controlled patching timelines. Attendees will learn how we addressed these risks through device hardening, using customer information system baselines, network segmentation, identity and access management improvements, and passive vulnerability monitoring. A key component of our success was our collaborative approach. The results speak for themselves: a 75-percent reduction in unknown edge devices, 45-percent increase in segmentation coverage, and measurable improvement in cross-departmental engagement.

Digital Health Transformation
TEFCA Update from the RCE

Add to schedule
In 2019, the Assistant Secretary for Technology Policy and Office of the National Coordinator for Health Information Technology (ASTP/ONC) awarded The Sequoia Project, and subcontractors including Carequality, a cooperative agreement to serve as the Recognized Coordinating Entity to help achieve the vision of a “network of networks.” In 2023, the contract was renewed for five more years. The RCE is responsible for developing, updating, implementing and maintaining the Common Agreement component of the Trusted Exchange Framework and Common Agreement™. The Common Agreement will create the baseline technical and legal requirements for health information networks to share electronic health information and is part of the 21st Century Cures Act. The speakers will review the current scope and requirements of the TEFCA™ and the progress made by the RCE in collaboration with the Assistant Secretary of Technology and Policy at the U.S. Department of Health and Human Services (HHS), to include the Common Agreement and the Qualified Health Information Network® (QHIN™) Technical Framework. Opportunities for stakeholder and community input will be presented.

The Organizational Analytics Capability Model Health Care Organization Self-Assessment Handbook

Add to schedule
In this workshop, the presenters will cover the Organizational Analytics Capability Model Health Care Organization Self-Assessment Handbook. Data has become a critical asset for organizations seeking to reduce costs and improve patient/client care, population health and staff experiences. Healthcare organizations, including Federally Qualified Health Centers, Certified Community Behavioral Health Clinics (CCBHCs) and hospitals, increasingly recognize the value of leveraging data analytics to inform decision-making and enhance care delivery. Organizational analytics capability refers to the sophistication with which an organization collects, manages, analyzes and applies data to achieve its strategic objectives. In this era of artificial intelligence-driven technology, lacking data analytics capacity puts organizations at risk of becoming obsolete. This handbook can be used as a guide to assess and enhance your organization’s analytics capability. This toolkit was developed in 2025 by Wellbeing in Action in partnership with the National Council for Mental Wellbeing’s CCBHC-E National Training and Technical Assistance Center. This workshop will cover the handbook and its implementation by healthcare organizations.

Defining and Implementing an AI-Ready Cyber Strategy

Add to schedule

Empowering Patients, Enabling Life-Saving Care: TEFCA, 360X Interoperability, and AI-Enabled IAS

Add to schedule
A 39-year-old woman with new psychiatric symptoms visits her PCP, who initiates a 360X closed-loop referral to psychiatry. As her symptoms rapidly progress, the psychiatrist identifies concern for an underlying life-threatening condition and urgently transfers her to the ED. In the ED, clinicians query her medical information using TEFCA QHIN-enabled interoperability. She receives timely treatment, makes a full recovery, and retains little memory of the acute event. After returning home, she logs into her HealthEx application. Her identity is verified through CLEAR, enabling secure access. Her data is retrieved via TEFCA interoperability, allowing her to view a comprehensive record of her care. Using AI-enabled tools within the application, she is able to clearly understand her medical history and what occurred during her illness.

INFRA Infection Radar: Blueprint for Data-Driven Calculation of Sepsis

Add to schedule
Different scoring systems are in use for assessing the severity of sepsis. In an interinstitutional project funded by the Swiss Personalized Health Network, a data-driven approach to assign the diagnosis sepsis was developed with respect to the different scores. Based on routine data from the electronic healthcare record, including the mapping to interoperable terminologies a blueprint could be set up and ready for reuse. FAIR principles were applied. The interoperable terminologies and classifications of SNOMED CT, LOINC, ICD 10, UCUM, and ATC were used. A data-pipeline was established to feed reporting tools in order to visualize the results for the clinicians, enhancing timely treatment. The data was also used for setting up predictive models, helping to detect patient groups at risk. An interdisciplinary team was involved of data analysts, data engineer, physicians, data manager, terminologist and bio informaticist. Among the institutions were two university hospitals and two data science centers. Data: laboratory, vitals, coding, administrative.

Preparing for the Unexpected Through Live Simulations

Add to schedule
Endorsed by: Between August 2024 and February 2025, live simulations depicting real-life clinical scenarios were conducted at each of our 10 campuses. The live simulations took real-life clinical scenarios (chest pains, stroke, gastrointestinal bleed, etc.), and enacted them in clinical areas such as the Emergency Department, inpatient medical/surgical and ICU units, along with radiology, pharmacy and blood bank under the circumstances that Epic, Rover and Haiku were done. The live simulations tested our current business continuity workflows and systems but also led to the discovery of numerous lessons. One key takeaway was that many of the staff working today have never worked in a paper system. We also realized that there was a lack of standardization of how we would admit patients, transfer patients, process medication orders, etc. One of our biggest key takeaways was we needed to build a robust communication method for our clinicians to speak to one another during a downtime. Live simulations offer a unique opportunity to test the reliability of what we have built in place for downtime readiness but also understand what else needs to be done in an unexpected prolonged downtime.

HL7 FHIR as the Engine for National Interoperability: The Italian NHS Case Study

Add to schedule

Accelerating Adoption of Value-Based Care with the CPT® Code Set

Add to schedule
The shift toward value-based care (VBC) has led to a reimagining of the traditional definition of healthcare delivery—including what types of services are delivered, how those services are delivered and by whom they are delivered—all with the objective of supporting better outcomes at lower costs. The American Medical Association (AMA), in collaboration with Manatt Health, set out to understand the role of Current Procedural Terminology (CPT®), the standard medical code set terminology for reporting medical services and procedures, in VBC. The key findings are that CPT® serves as the common language for VBC today and is a critical enabler of the three pillars of VBC success going forward: population health and quality management, cost management, and alternative payment model contracting.

Digital Health Transformation
Five Years of Transforming Access: Brazil’s Large-Scale Specialty Teleconsultation Program

Add to schedule
To combat deep-seated health disparities, Brazil launched one of the Global South's largest teleconsultation initiatives, the TeleAMES project. Over the past five years, this program, led by Hospital Israelita Albert Einstein under the Ministry of Health's PROADI-SUS framework, has become a powerful tool for health equity. It delivered more than 387,526 specialty consultations directly to 401 underserved municipalities across 10 of Brazil's most remote states in the North and Midwest regions. The model was designed to dismantle barriers to access. It significantly reduced the financial and logistical burdens on patients who would otherwise travel long distances for care. The initiative achieved remarkable engagement, with a 96.81-percent appointment occupancy rate and high satisfaction (NPS: 91 for physicians, 85 for patients). This session presents a proven blueprint for leveraging telemedicine to advance health equity in public health systems. We will demonstrate how our model—integrating structured digital workflows, clinical protocols and robust quality control—successfully bridged geographic and social divides. The discussion will share critical lessons on achieving high continuity and equitable coverage despite infrastructure challenges, offering a replicable framework for any nation aiming to reduce structural inequalities and deliver quality healthcare to its most vulnerable populations.

Revisioning Brain Cancer Care Delivery through Digital Transformation

Add to schedule
At Mayo Clinic, the Neuro-Oncology Anywhere clinical trial portfolio is transforming how brain cancer care is delivered. Using telehealth visits, remote patient education services, device-based patient monitoring technologies, digital chemotherapy toxicity checks, home or local phlebotomy services, mail-order drug delivery, and virtual tumor boards, the Neuro-Oncology Anywhere clinical trials are bringing brain cancer care to patients' homes. The platform started with remote cognitive assessments for patients who have received intracranial radiation therapy. With its latest iteration, the Neuro-Oncology Anywhere portfolio now includes home chemotherapy services that allows for administration of both conventional and experimental therapeutics without need for patient travel. The digital platform created by these clinical trials is accelerating drug development and testing while simultaneously making access to care easier for individuals with brain cancer.

Business and Financial Management
Streamlining EHR Onboarding: Enhancing Efficiency and Retention Through Adaptive Learning

Add to schedule
KLAS Research Company’s assessments show that longer length of initial EHR training is strongly correlated with EHR satisfaction. However, 80 percent of new personnel are experienced with EHRs, and training efficiency and effectiveness are goals shared by the learner and the healthcare organization. Our goal was to create a self-paced, learner-centered program to reduce training time, speed up clinical readiness and improve retention for learners. A blended learning approach was implemented, combining instructor-led sessions and self-paced modules, using computer adaptive learning (CAL) to personalize the experience. Six provider and nursing courses were piloted. CAL ensured learners demonstrated mastery before completing eLearning modules, with analytics identifying areas needing further support. The project focused on changing platforms and methodologies, leveraging existing training content. The optimized onboarding process reduced training time significantly—provider eLearning time decreased by one hour, and classroom time was cut from 4–16 hours to 2 hours. The RN course shifted from 4 hours of classroom time to 2 hours of self-paced learning. Training retention assessments showed statistically significant improvements for RNs and a positive trend for providers. Reduced time in training yielded a 200-percent return on investment. Future efforts will focus on broadened implementation, refining post-onboarding support and continuous improvement.

Business and Financial Management
The Pros and Cons of Performing Security Assessments Under Privilege

Add to schedule
A security assessment, such as a HIPAA Security Rule risk analysis, can reveal all of an organizations greatest vulnerabilities. In the hands of a hacker, it can serve as a roadmap of how to attack the organization. In the hands of a plaintiff’s attorney or regulator, it can serve as damning evidence of information security failures. In 2024, the Federal Trade Commission placed a healthcare provider under a 20-year consent order for deceptive trade practices because it claimed that it was HIPAA-compliant but the results of its independent HIPAA gap assessment found only 60-percent compliance. One method to protect the confidentiality of a risk assessment or compliance review is to conduct it under the direction of legal counsel and claim the benefit of attorney-client privilege. This session will explore the pros and cons of such an approach, such as the benefits of a claim of privilege; the extra time, cost, and burden of involving legal counsel; and the risks that a claim of privilege will fail and the assessment will be used against the organization. The session also will discuss the operational elements of performing an assessment under the direction of counsel, with practical tips and strategies.
Mar 10, 2026, 3:30 PM to 4:30 PM

When Risk Becomes Visible: How Predictive Models Can Impact Care

Add to schedule
Despite the promise of predictive analytics in critical care units, few applications have achieved widespread clinical adoption. Generalizability, proven outcomes and clinical integration remain persistent challenges, especially for systems with machine learning models that use only electronic health record (EHR), which may reflect clinical response rather than the underlying physiological state of the patient. In this session, we describe a successful alternative: predictive models that emphasize continuous cardiorespiratory monitoring data, developed using rigorous time-series analytics and clinician-validated outcomes. Recent successes include a reduction in cardiac arrests without return of spontaneous circulation in the Pediatric Intensive Care Unit. These models, which report on patient physiology rather than provider behavior, generalize across patient populations, hospital units and time periods, with no apparent drift or systematic error. They are currently in clinical use and are integrated into routine bedside workflows. We will describe lessons learned from real-world deployment, emphasizing collaboration with clinicians at the onset and the need for an adaptable platform that supports algorithm development, testing and display. This approach offers a path forward for predictive analytics monitoring by combining continuous signal-rich data, robust analytical methods and thoughtful integration to deliver on its original promise.

Building Trust and Confidence Through Better Healthcare Data Quality and Usability

Add to schedule
In today's interconnected healthcare landscape, data flows across providers, public health agencies and patient portals—but trust only emerges when the data is reliable, usable and secure. Leveraging the Sequoia Project’s Data Usability Workgroup Implementation Guide Version 2.0, released December 11, 2024, this session explores seven critical focus areas—from provenance and code use to reducing duplicates and ensuring data integrity—that directly underpin trustworthiness. Participants will gain a roadmap to enhance systems and workflows through practical tech-agnostic guidance aligned with United States Core Data for Interoperability (USCDI) version 3 and HL7® standards. We will dive into how the Data Usability Taking Root Community of Practice has leveraged structured provenance tracking, standardized coding, narrative linkage, lab interoperability and metadata tagging, which all contribute to data’s integrity—and to the clinician and patient confidence it inspires. Attendees will leave equipped with clear, actionable strategies and implementation steps that can be adopted by vendors, implementers and electronic health information exchanges (HIEs) within 18 months, as envisioned in the guide. With USCDI version 3 adoption starting in 2026, plus growing expectations for data insight tools and artificial intelligence, there is no better time to build the foundation of trusted data. The Implementation Guide version 2.0 delivers pragmatic, reliable healthcare data—fueling better decisions and stronger patient trust.

Didi Davis
The Sequoia Project
Digital Health Transformation
Decreasing Unwarranted Clinical Variation to Improve Outcomes and Reduce Costs

Add to schedule
Health systems continue to face challenges in reducing unwarranted clinical variation, contributing to higher costs, inconsistent outcomes and wasted resources. This session explores a scalable, data-driven approach to clinical variation reduction, enabled by advanced analytics and supported by strong governance and provider engagement. Attendees will learn how a multisite healthcare system integrated data from disparate electronic healthcare records and billing systems into a unified analytics platform to generate real-time insights and identify high-priority areas for intervention. Using tools such as Key Process Analysis and condition-specific accelerators for sepsis and heart failure, the organization targeted improvement opportunities with the highest potential for impact. The initiative achieved measurable results, including significant reductions in sepsis and heart failure mortality, improved resource utilization, and greater clinician alignment around shared quality goals. The session will outline how clinical leadership, transparent data and tailored improvement frameworks contributed to sustained change. Participants will gain practical insights into designing and implementing a successful variation reduction program, including lessons learned, reproducible strategies and key enablers of success. The session is ideal for leaders looking to advance their organization’s analytics maturity, scale improvement efforts and deliver more consistent, high-value care.

Greenway Health
Empowering Patients, Enabling Life-Saving Care: TEFCA, 360X Interoperability, and AI-Enabled IAS

Add to schedule
A 39-year-old woman with new psychiatric symptoms visits her PCP, who initiates a 360X closed-loop referral to psychiatry. As her symptoms rapidly progress, the psychiatrist identifies concern for an underlying life-threatening condition and urgently transfers her to the ED. In the ED, clinicians query her medical information using TEFCA QHIN-enabled interoperability. She receives timely treatment, makes a full recovery, and retains little memory of the acute event. After returning home, she logs into her HealthEx application. Her identity is verified through CLEAR, enabling secure access. Her data is retrieved via TEFCA interoperability, allowing her to view a comprehensive record of her care. Using AI-enabled tools within the application, she is able to clearly understand her medical history and what occurred during her illness.

Evaluating the Efficacy and Future of Mental Health Apps

Add to schedule
As digital mental health solutions proliferate, stakeholders (including healthcare systems, payers, and mental health practitioners) face increasing pressure to distinguish clinically meaningful tools from those lacking evidence, integration capability, or ethical safeguards. This session will provide insight into how payers and providers consider digital mental health solutions and presents a structured evaluation framework for mental health apps, grounded in principles of clinical efficacy, privacy and security, patient-centered usability, and accessibility.Since 2019, APA has hosted the App Evaluation Framework, designed to employ a hierarchical rating system and embedded rubric to guide physicians, mental health professionals and patients in evaluating apps, highlighting key differences from choosing more traditional therapeutic interventions.Providers, health plans and other stakeholders will discuss the importance of developing standards that allow decision-makers to identify apps suitable for clinical integration that emphasize evidence based medical appropriateness, privacy practices, health equity, and engagement.Attendees will gain actionable strategies to evaluate, select, and implement mental health apps that align with organizational goals and care outcomes.
